Impossibility Due to External Prevention: The Example of Two Agents
The author describes the example of two conflicting agents to illustrate impossibility due to external prevention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how impossibility can arise from external prevention rather than from the thing itself, and see the example used by the author.

Core Idea
External prevention causes real incapacity, not intrinsic impossibility.

The author begins his critique of a false analogy by presenting a clear example: if two beings each have power over intrinsically possible things, one might prevent the other from achieving its goal. This results in a real inability, which is a sign of weakness. This example sets the stage for distinguishing such external prevention from intrinsic impossibility, which we will examine in the next lesson.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on external prevention
Read the Arabic and translation describing the two-agent scenario. Pay attention to the phrases: 'مقدور في نفسه' (possible in itself) and 'لمنع صاحبه' (due to prevention of the other).
This is the first part of the author's argument.
2
Identify the key terms
Note the terms: قدرة (power), مقدور (possible), تعجيز (disabling). See how they are used.
3
Understand the consequence
The author concludes that the inability here is due to the other's prevention, not because the act itself is impossible. This is a form of incapacity (عجز).
Contrast with the next lesson where impossibility is intrinsic.
4
Ponder the theological implications
Consider why this distinction matters for discussions of God's power. Could external prevention apply to God? Why or why not?
This will be answered in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذي يدل على بطلان كلامه وبعد استشهاده أنه شبه هذا باستحالة ثبوت القدرة على ظلمه أو كذبه وهو غاية الجهالة، فإنا صورنا ثبوت قدرة كل واحد منهما على ما لا يستحيل ثبوت القدرة عليه، لولا منع صاحبه إياه، فإن أحدهما إذا أراد إثبات السواد في محل أو إثبات الحركة والحياة فيه فقد أراد إثبات ما هو مقدور في نفسه، إذ السواد والحركة والحياة داخلة تحت القدرة لولا تحصیل صاحبه أضدادها، فحيث لم يقدر على إثباتها فإنما لم يقدر لمنع صاحبه إياه عن تنفيذ مراده، فكان هذا من صاحبه تعجيزا له وكذا على القلب، فأما وجود الكذب من الباري عز وجل ففي حيز المستحيلات لما أن صدقه تعالى أزلي ممتنع العدم ولا وجه لوجود كذبه مع وجود صدقه لاستحالة اجتماعهما ولا وجه إلى القول بانعدام الصدق ليثبت الكذب لاستحالة العدم على الأزلي لكونه واجب الوجود وانتفاء القدرة عما يستحيل دخوله تحت القدرة لا يكون عن عجز ، بل لخروج المحل عن أن يكون قابلا للقدرة فلا ثبوت للعجز الذي هو نقيصة منافية للقدم، فأما انتفاء القدرة عما هو مقدور في نفسه فلم يكن لامتناع المحل قبوله فكان لثبوت ما يضادها وهو العجز الذي هو من أمارات الحدث، فمن قاس خروج الحركة أو الحياة أو السواد ليس في أنفسها ما يمتنع عن قبول القدرة بخروج الكذب، مع أنه في نفسه ما يوجب امتناعه عن قبول القدرة فهو جاهل بشرائط القياس، غير بصير بالفرق بين المحال والممكن
And what proves the invalidity of his statement and the weakness of his citation is that he likened this to the impossibility of affirming power over injustice or lying, which is the height of ignorance. For we conceived the affirmation of the power of each of them over that for which the affirmation of power is not impossible, were it not for the prevention of the other from him. For if one of them wishes to establish blackness in a place or to establish motion and life in it, he wishes to establish that which is possible in itself, since blackness, motion, and life fall under power were it not for the other bringing about their opposites. So when he is not able to establish them, he is only unable due to the prevention of the other from him from executing his will. So this is from the other a disabling of him, and similarly conversely. As for the occurrence of lying from the Exalted and Majestic, it is in the realm of impossibilities because His truthfulness is eternal, impossible of non-existence, and there is no way for the existence of His lying with the existence of His truthfulness due to the impossibility of their coexistence, and there is no way to say that truthfulness is annihilated so that lying is affirmed, due to the impossibility of non-existence for the eternal because He is necessary of existence. And the absence of power over that which it is impossible to come under power is not due to incapacity, but because the locus is not receptive to power; so there is no affirmation of incapacity which is a deficiency contrary to pre-eternity. As for the absence of power over that which is possible in itself, it was not due to the locus's refusal to accept it, but due to the existence of what is opposite to it, which is incapacity, which is one of the signs of contingency. So whoever analogizes the exclusion of motion or life or blackness—which in themselves are not impossible to accept power—with the exclusion of lying, while it (lying) in itself necessitates its impossibility to accept power, is ignorant of the conditions of analogy, unseeing of the difference between the impossible and the possible.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage explains the distinction between two types of impossibility. The author points out that the opponent compared the impossibility of two gods having power over each other to the impossibility of God having power over lying or injustice, which is a false analogy. The author breaks down the example: if two beings existed, each could have power over things that are intrinsically possible, like blackness or motion, but the other could prevent it, resulting in a disabling (تعجيز) that implies weakness. In contrast, God's lying is impossible not because of external prevention but because lying is intrinsically impossible for God due to His eternal truthfulness and the impossibility of change in His attributes. The absence of power over lying is not due to incapacity but because lying cannot be an object of power. However, the absence of power over intrinsically possible things (like blackness when prevented) is due to incapacity, a mark of contingency. Thus, the opponent fails to see the difference between the impossible in itself and the possible that is prevented.

Key Terms
شبهة
قدرة
مقدور
عجز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of two agents, why is one agent unable to establish blackness?
A) Because blackness is intrinsically impossible.
B) Because the other agent brings about its opposite.
C) Because the agent lacks power.
D) Because blackness cannot be an object of power.

Key Takeaway
Impossibility can be due to external prevention, which involves real incapacity, not intrinsic impossibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Are you using 'external prevention' as an excuse to avoid effort, or are you honestly recognizing genuine incapacity?

Intrinsic Impossibility: The Case of God's Lying
The author explains why God's lying is intrinsically impossible and criticizes the false analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's inability to lie is due to intrinsic impossibility, not weakness, and why the opponent's analogy violates the conditions of valid qiyas.

Core Idea
Intrinsic impossibility is not a matter of power; absence of power over it is not incapacity.

Now the author turns to the core of his argument: God's lying is impossible not because of external prevention, but because it is intrinsically impossible. He explains that God's eternal truthfulness precludes the possibility of lying, as it would require a change in God's essential attributes. Therefore, the absence of power over lying is not a sign of weakness but a logical necessity. The author concludes by criticizing the opponent's failure to observe the conditions of analogy (شرائط القياس).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on intrinsic impossibility
Read the Arabic and translation from 'فأما وجود الكذب' to the end. Note the phrases: 'محال', 'مستحيل', 'لا يدخل تحت القدرة'.
This is the second part of the author's argument.
2
Analyze the reasoning
The author gives two reasons: (1) God's truthfulness is eternal and cannot cease to exist, so lying cannot coexist with it. (2) The absence of power over lying is not due to incapacity but because the locus (God's essence) is not receptive to lying.
See how the author distinguishes between two types of absence of power.
3
Contrast with the previous example
In the previous example, the object was possible in itself but prevented; here the object is impossible in itself. Thus, the analogy between them is invalid.
4
Understand the conditions of qiyas
The author says the opponent is ignorant of the conditions of qiyas. Explain why the analogy fails: the two cases are not comparable because the nature of the objects is different.
This highlights the importance of proper reasoning in theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذي يدل على بطلان كلامه وبعد استشهاده أنه شبه هذا باستحالة ثبوت القدرة على ظلمه أو كذبه وهو غاية الجهالة، فإنا صورنا ثبوت قدرة كل واحد منهما على ما لا يستحيل ثبوت القدرة عليه، لولا منع صاحبه إياه، فإن أحدهما إذا أراد إثبات السواد في محل أو إثبات الحركة والحياة فيه فقد أراد إثبات ما هو مقدور في نفسه، إذ السواد والحركة والحياة داخلة تحت القدرة لولا تحصیل صاحبه أضدادها، فحيث لم يقدر على إثباتها فإنما لم يقدر لمنع صاحبه إياه عن تنفيذ مراده، فكان هذا من صاحبه تعجيزا له وكذا على القلب، فأما وجود الكذب من الباري عز وجل ففي حيز المستحيلات لما أن صدقه تعالى أزلي ممتنع العدم ولا وجه لوجود كذبه مع وجود صدقه لاستحالة اجتماعهما ولا وجه إلى القول بانعدام الصدق ليثبت الكذب لاستحالة العدم على الأزلي لكونه واجب الوجود وانتفاء القدرة عما يستحيل دخوله تحت القدرة لا يكون عن عجز ، بل لخروج المحل عن أن يكون قابلا للقدرة فلا ثبوت للعجز الذي هو نقيصة منافية للقدم، فأما انتفاء القدرة عما هو مقدور في نفسه فلم يكن لامتناع المحل قبوله فكان لثبوت ما يضادها وهو العجز الذي هو من أمارات الحدث، فمن قاس خروج الحركة أو الحياة أو السواد ليس في أنفسها ما يمتنع عن قبول القدرة بخروج الكذب، مع أنه في نفسه ما يوجب امتناعه عن قبول القدرة فهو جاهل بشرائط القياس، غير بصير بالفرق بين المحال والممكن
And what proves the invalidity of his statement and the weakness of his citation is that he likened this to the impossibility of affirming power over injustice or lying, which is the height of ignorance. For we conceived the affirmation of the power of each of them over that for which the affirmation of power is not impossible, were it not for the prevention of the other from him. For if one of them wishes to establish blackness in a place or to establish motion and life in it, he wishes to establish that which is possible in itself, since blackness, motion, and life fall under power were it not for the other bringing about their opposites. So when he is not able to establish them, he is only unable due to the prevention of the other from him from executing his will. So this is from the other a disabling of him, and similarly conversely. As for the occurrence of lying from the Exalted and Majestic, it is in the realm of impossibilities because His truthfulness is eternal, impossible of non-existence, and there is no way for the existence of His lying with the existence of His truthfulness due to the impossibility of their coexistence, and there is no way to say that truthfulness is annihilated so that lying is affirmed, due to the impossibility of non-existence for the eternal because He is necessary of existence. And the absence of power over that which it is impossible to come under power is not due to incapacity, but because the locus is not receptive to power; so there is no affirmation of incapacity which is a deficiency contrary to pre-eternity. As for the absence of power over that which is possible in itself, it was not due to the locus's refusal to accept it, but due to the existence of what is opposite to it, which is incapacity, which is one of the signs of contingency. So whoever analogizes the exclusion of motion or life or blackness—which in themselves are not impossible to accept power—with the exclusion of lying, while it (lying) in itself necessitates its impossibility to accept power, is ignorant of the conditions of analogy, unseeing of the difference between the impossible and the possible.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage explains the distinction between two types of impossibility. The author points out that the opponent compared the impossibility of two gods having power over each other to the impossibility of God having power over lying or injustice, which is a false analogy. The author breaks down the example: if two beings existed, each could have power over things that are intrinsically possible, like blackness or motion, but the other could prevent it, resulting in a disabling (تعجيز) that implies weakness. In contrast, God's lying is impossible not because of external prevention but because lying is intrinsically impossible for God due to His eternal truthfulness and the impossibility of change in His attributes. The absence of power over lying is not due to incapacity but because lying cannot be an object of power. However, the absence of power over intrinsically possible things (like blackness when prevented) is due to incapacity, a mark of contingency. Thus, the opponent fails to see the difference between the impossible in itself and the possible that is prevented.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God cannot do something, it implies weakness or incapacity.
Correction: God's inability to perform intrinsically impossible acts like lying is not due to weakness but because such acts cannot logically be objects of power.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is the absence of power over lying not a sign of incapacity in God?
A) Because God is powerful enough to lie but chooses not to.
B) Because lying is impossible in itself and cannot come under power.
C) Because God lacks the ability to lie.
D) Because lying is prevented by another being.

Key Takeaway
Intrinsic impossibility means the thing cannot be an object of power; absence of power over it is not incapacity but a logical necessity.

Impossibility of Injustice and Lying for God (Maturidi View)
Maturidi argument on injustice and lying impossibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidi school argues that injustice and lying are impossible attributes of God.

Core Idea
God's eternal justice makes injustice impossible as an attribute.

This passage presents the Maturidi argument that injustice cannot be an attribute of God because His eternal action is justice and beneficence. The author draws a parallel with lying, showing that these are not merely impossible acts but that their impossibility is rooted in the divine nature itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the logical flow.
2
Identify the argument
Notice that the author states that injustice is impossible because God's action is eternal justice.
This is a conceptual impossibility, not a lack of power.
3
Compare with lying
The author says it is 'just as in the case of lying' — draw the parallel.
Lying is also impossible for God, not because He lacks power but because truth is necessary for Him.
4
Contrast with motion and rest
The author notes that for motion and rest the matter is different. Why?
This shows that not all contingent attributes are impossible for God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا صيرورة الظلم صفة الله تعالى محال لما أن فعله الأزلي عدل، وإفضال عندنا، ويمتنع قيام الظلم به مع وجود ذلك، ويستحيل على ذلك العدم، فكان محالا كما في الكذب، فأما في الحركة والسكون فالأمر بخلافه على ما بينا، وعند الأشعري فالقدرة على محال لما أن الظلم هو التعدي في الفعل عما جعل له، وارتكاب المنهي، ولا نهي لأحد على الله تعالى، فالقدرة على الظلم تستحيل، لأنها قدرة على إثبات ولاية الأمر والنهي لغير الله تعالى عليه، وإدخاله تحت قهر غيره، وهذا كله محال ممتنع ، فأما ما ألزمنا فليس بممتنع في نفسه، فكان انتفاء القدرة عن عجز فيه وقهر لصاحبه عليه حيث منعه عن إثبات مقدوره، والعجز من أمارات الحدث وهو منافى للربوبية، وفيما ألزم هو الأمر بخلافه على ما قررنا
And similarly, the becoming of injustice as an attribute of God is impossible because His eternal action is justice and beneficence according to us, and it is impossible for injustice to subsist in Him with the existence of that (justice), and non-existence is impossible for that (justice), so it is impossible just as in the case of lying. As for in motion and rest, the matter is otherwise, as we have explained. And according to al-Ash‘ari, power over the impossible does not apply because injustice is transgression in action beyond what is prescribed for it and committing what is prohibited, and there is no prohibition upon God from anyone, so power over injustice is impossible because it would be power to affirm authority of command and prohibition over God for other than God, and to bring Him under the coercion of another. All of this is impossible and prevented. As for what we have required (in the case of two gods), it is not impossible in itself. So the absence of power (there) was due to incapacity and the coercion of the other over him, where he prevented him from establishing his possible act, and incapacity is one of the signs of contingency and is contrary to lordship. And in what he required (the analogy), the matter is contrary as we have established.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage concludes the distinction by focusing on the impossibility of injustice and lying for God. The author states that injustice cannot become an attribute of God because His eternal action is justice and beneficence; it is impossible for injustice to coexist with that, and the eternal justice cannot cease. So it is like lying. In contrast, motion and rest are not impossible. Then the author presents the Ash‘ari perspective: power over the impossible is not applicable because injustice involves transgression and prohibition, and there is no prohibition on God. Claiming power over injustice would imply someone else having authority over God, which is impossible. However, in the case of the two gods (the opponent's objection), the absence of power was due to incapacity and coercion, which are signs of contingency, not a problem of intrinsic impossibility. The author thus refutes the false analogy by showing that the type of impossibility is different.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God cannot commit injustice, He is not all-powerful.
Correction: The passage clarifies that injustice is not a possible object of power; it is a conceptual impossibility, not a limitation. God's power is only over possible things.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main reason for saying injustice is impossible for God?
A) Because God willed it to be impossible.
B) Because God's eternal action is justice and beneficence.
C) Because God lacks the power to commit injustice.
D) Because injustice leads to harm in creation.

Key Takeaway
Injustice and lying are impossible for God because they conflict with His eternal attributes of justice and truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage equates the impossibility of injustice with that of lying. In what ways do you tolerate small 'injustices' in your own character (e.g., partiality, unfair criticism) as if they were possible for you? How can you use the truth of God's perfect justice as a model to repent and pursue greater fairness in your dealings with others?

Ash'ari Perspective and Refutation of the Two Gods Analogy
Ash'ari view on injustice impossibility and refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari argument against the possibility of injustice for God and how the author refutes the analogy of two gods.

Core Idea
Power over injustice implies external authority over God, which is impossible.

This passage shifts to the Ash'ari perspective, which argues that power over injustice is impossible because injustice involves transgression and there is no prohibition on God. The author then addresses an objection about two gods, showing that the type of impossibility there is different—it stems from incapacity and coercion, not intrinsic impossibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the Ash'ari argument
Read how al-Ash'ari argues that power over the impossible does not apply to injustice because there is no prohibition on God.
2
Notice the reasoning
The passage says that claiming power over injustice would mean affirming someone else's authority over God.
This is the core of the argument.
3
Understand the refutation
The author rejects the analogy that if two gods existed, each would lack power over the other's actions.
The impossibility in that case is due to incapacity, not intrinsic impossibility.
4
Contrast the two types of impossibility
Distinguish between impossibility due to intrinsic nature (injustice) and impossibility due to external coercion (two gods).
This is crucial for understanding the author's response.

The Impossibility of Lying for Allah
Al-Nasafi argues that lying is impossible for Allah due to eternal truthfulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why lying is impossible for Allah based on the eternity of His truthfulness and the nature of divine power.

Core Idea
Lying is impossible for Allah because His truthfulness is eternal and cannot cease.

Imam al-Nasafi begins by establishing that lying cannot be attributed to Allah. He argues that Allah's truthfulness is an eternal attribute, and since the eternal cannot be negated, lying cannot coexist with it. The absence of power over lying is not a deficiency but because lying is inherently impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on lying
Read the Arabic passage focusing on how al-Nasafi defines the impossibility of lying. Notice the key terms: كذب, صدق, أزلي.
The passage uses a conditional structure: if truthfulness is eternal, lying cannot exist.
2
Understand the eternal truthfulness argument
Al-Nasafi states that Allah's truthfulness (sidq) is eternal and cannot cease. Therefore, lying (kadhib) cannot exist alongside it. The idea of truthfulness ceasing is impossible because the eternal cannot be negated.
This relies on the concept of wajib al-wujud (necessary existence) for eternal attributes.
3
Analyze the negation of power
The passage explains that the lack of power over lying is not due to incapacity (cajz), but because the thing itself (lying) is not a possible object of power. Incapacity would be a deficiency, but here the subject is simply not receptive.
Distinguish between 'not possible' (muhal) and 'possible but lacking power' (which would imply incapacity).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فكان هذا من صاحبه تعجيزا له وكذا على القلب، فأما وجود الكذب من الباري عز وجل ففي حيز المستحيلات لما أن صدقه تعالى أزلي ممتنع العدم (ولا وجه لوجود كذبه مع وجود صدقه لاستحالة اجتماعهما) ولا وجه إلى القول بانعدام الصدق ليثبت الكذب لاستحالة العدم على الأزلي لكونه واجب الوجود وانتفاء القدرة) عما يستحيل دخوله تحت القدرة لا يكون عن عجز ، بل لخروج المحل عن أن يكون قابلا للقدرة فلا ثبوت للعجز الذي هو نقيصة منافية للقدم، فأما انتفاء القدرة عما هو مقدور في نفسه فلم يكن لامتناع المحل قبوله فكان لثبوت ما يضادها وهو العجز الذي هو من أمارات الحدث، فمن قاس خروج الحركة أو الحياة أو السواد ليس في أنفسها ما يمتنع عن قبول القدرة بخروج الكذب، مع أنه في نفسه ما يوجب امتناعه عن قبول القدرة فهو جاهل بشرائط القياس، غير بصير بالفرق بين المحال والممكن، وكذا صيرورة الظلم صفة الله تعالى محال لما أن فعله الأزلي عدل، وإفضال عندنا، ويمتنع قيام الظلم به مع وجود ذلك، ويستحيل على ذلك العدم، فكان محالا كما في الكذب، فأما في الحركة والسكون فالأمر بخلافه على ما بينا، وعند الأشعري فالقدرة على محال لما أن الظلم هو التعدي في الفعل عما جعل له، وارتكاب المنهي، ولا نهي لأحد على الله تعالى، فالقدرة على الظلم تستحيل، لأنها قدرة على إثبات ولاية الأمر والنهي لغير الله تعالى عليه، وإدخاله تحت قهر غيره، وهذا كله محال ممتنع ، فأما ما ألزمنا فليس بممتنع في نفسه، فكان انتفاء القدرة عن عجز فيه وقهر لصاحبه عليه حيث منعه عن إثبات مقدوره، والعجز من أمارات الحدث وهو منافى للربوبية، وفيما ألزم هو الأمر بخلافه على ما قررنا.
So this was from its owner a declaration of incapacity for him, and likewise on the reverse. As for the existence of lying from Allah, Blessed and Exalted, it is in the realm of impossibilities because His truthfulness, Exalted, is eternal, impossible of non-existence. (And there is no way for the existence of His lying with the existence of His truthfulness because of the impossibility of their co-existence.) And there is no way to say that truthfulness ceases to exist to establish lying, because of the impossibility of non-existence for the eternal, due to its being necessary of existence, and the negation of power over what is impossible to enter under power is not due to incapacity, but because the subject is not receptive to power. So there is no affirmation of incapacity, which is a deficiency incompatible with eternity. As for the negation of power over what is inherently possible, that is not because the subject refuses to accept it, but because of the affirmation of what opposes it, which is incapacity, which is one of the signs of contingency. Whoever analogizes the absence of motion or life or blackness—which in themselves do not prevent acceptance of power—to the absence of lying, whilst it is in itself that which necessitates its prevention from accepting power, is ignorant of the conditions of analogy, not discerning the difference between the impossible and the possible. Likewise, making injustice a attribute of Allah is impossible because His eternal action is justice and beneficence according to us, and it is impossible for injustice to subsist in Him with the existence of that, and its non-existence is impossible, so it is impossible just as in the case of lying. As for motion and rest, the matter is contrary to what we have explained. According to al-Ash'ari, power over the impossible is because injustice is transgression in action from what has been appointed for it and committing what is prohibited, and there is no prohibition for anyone over Allah. So power over injustice is impossible, because it is power to establish the authority of commanding and forbidding for other than Allah over Him, and to bring Him under the coercion of another. All of this is impossible and prevented. As for what we have obliged, it is not impossible in itself. So the negation of power was not due to incapacity in it and coercion of its possessor over him, where it prevents him from establishing his capability. Incapacity is one of the signs of contingency and is incompatible with lordship. In what is obliged, the matter is contrary to what we have established.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage presents a complex argument about the impossibility of lying (kadhib) and injustice (zulm) being attributes of Allah. The author, Imam al-Nasafi, first states that lying is impossible for Allah because His truthfulness is eternal and cannot cease. Even if one were to argue that truthfulness could be removed for lying to occur, that is impossible because the eternal cannot be negated. The lack of power (qudra) over such an impossible thing is not due to incapacity (cajz), but because the thing itself is not a possible object of power. However, when power is absent for something that is inherently possible (maqdur fi nafsihi), that would indicate incapacity, which is a sign of contingency (hadath). The author then criticizes those who analogize the absence of contingent attributes (like motion) from inanimate objects (which are not receptive) to the absence of lying from Allah, pointing out the difference between the impossible (muhal) and the possible (mumkin). Next, the same reasoning is applied to injustice: Allah's actions are eternally just and beneficent, so injustice cannot subsist in Him. The author then presents the Ash'ari perspective, which holds that power over the impossible (such as injustice) is impossible because injustice would entail subjecting Allah to another's authority and prohibition, which is contradictory to lordship. Finally, al-Nasafi distinguishes between the negation of power due to the impossibility of the object (which does not imply deficiency) and the negation of power over a possible object (which would imply incapacity and is therefore not applicable to Allah).

صدق
أزلي
وجوب الوجود

قدرة
عجز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Allah's inability to lie is a limitation or weakness.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the 'inability' is because lying is inherently impossible, not because Allah lacks power. It is similar to the impossibility of creating a square circle; it is not a deficiency.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is lying impossible for Allah?
A) Because Allah's truthfulness is eternal and cannot cease.
B) Because Allah is merciful and cannot lie.
C) Because lying would require a body.
D) Because the Quran says so.

Key Takeaway
Lying is impossible for Allah because His truthfulness is eternal, and the lack of power over an impossible object does not imply incapacity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's truthfulness is eternal and cannot cease, what does that mean for every promise He has made to you in the Quran? Is there a specific promise you have been hesitant to rely on? What one action will you take this week to act on that promise as if it is absolutely certain?
?
The passage teaches that Allah's inability to lie is not a deficiency but a perfection. Think of a limitation you view as a weakness in yourself. Could it be that this 'limitation' is actually a sign of a greater perfection? How might reframing it change how you live today?
?
Since Allah cannot lie, His words are the ultimate truth. When you read the Quran, do you sometimes read with a heart that questions or negotiates with His commands? In which area of your life are you most tempted to treat Allah's statements as less than absolute truth? What will you do to surrender to His truth starting now?

The Impossibility of Injustice for Allah
Al-Nasafi argues that injustice is impossible for Allah using the same reasoning as for lying.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why injustice is impossible for Allah, using reasoning parallel to the impossibility of lying.

Core Idea
Injustice is impossible for Allah because His actions are eternally just and beneficent.

Imam al-Nasafi applies the same logical framework to the attribute of injustice (zulm). Since Allah's actions are inherently just and good, injustice cannot be attributed to Him. The reasoning mirrors the argument for lying: an eternal attribute (justice) precludes its opposite, and the non-existence of justice is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on injustice
Read the Arabic passage where al-Nasafi discusses injustice. Notice how he parallels the argument from lying.
The phrase 'كما في الكذب' (as in the case of lying) shows the same logic.
2
Understand the eternal justice argument
Al-Nasafi asserts that Allah's action (fi'l) is eternally just (adl) and beneficent (ifdal). Therefore, injustice cannot subsist in Him. If justice is eternal and cannot cease, injustice cannot exist.
This relies on the same principle of impossibility of opposites coexisting and the eternal not ceasing.
3
Compare with the lying argument
Notice the structural similarity: both arguments use the eternity of a positive attribute (truthfulness/justice) to preclude the negative attribute (lying/injustice). The negation of power is again attributed to the impossibility of the object, not to incapacity.
This shows a consistent method in kalam: using eternal attributes to negate their opposites.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فكان هذا من صاحبه تعجيزا له وكذا على القلب، فأما وجود الكذب من الباري عز وجل ففي حيز المستحيلات لما أن صدقه تعالى أزلي ممتنع العدم (ولا وجه لوجود كذبه مع وجود صدقه لاستحالة اجتماعهما) ولا وجه إلى القول بانعدام الصدق ليثبت الكذب لاستحالة العدم على الأزلي لكونه واجب الوجود وانتفاء القدرة) عما يستحيل دخوله تحت القدرة لا يكون عن عجز ، بل لخروج المحل عن أن يكون قابلا للقدرة فلا ثبوت للعجز الذي هو نقيصة منافية للقدم، فأما انتفاء القدرة عما هو مقدور في نفسه فلم يكن لامتناع المحل قبوله فكان لثبوت ما يضادها وهو العجز الذي هو من أمارات الحدث، فمن قاس خروج الحركة أو الحياة أو السواد ليس في أنفسها ما يمتنع عن قبول القدرة بخروج الكذب، مع أنه في نفسه ما يوجب امتناعه عن قبول القدرة فهو جاهل بشرائط القياس، غير بصير بالفرق بين المحال والممكن، وكذا صيرورة الظلم صفة الله تعالى محال لما أن فعله الأزلي عدل، وإفضال عندنا، ويمتنع قيام الظلم به مع وجود ذلك، ويستحيل على ذلك العدم، فكان محالا كما في الكذب، فأما في الحركة والسكون فالأمر بخلافه على ما بينا، وعند الأشعري فالقدرة على محال لما أن الظلم هو التعدي في الفعل عما جعل له، وارتكاب المنهي، ولا نهي لأحد على الله تعالى، فالقدرة على الظلم تستحيل، لأنها قدرة على إثبات ولاية الأمر والنهي لغير الله تعالى عليه، وإدخاله تحت قهر غيره، وهذا كله محال ممتنع ، فأما ما ألزمنا فليس بممتنع في نفسه، فكان انتفاء القدرة عن عجز فيه وقهر لصاحبه عليه حيث منعه عن إثبات مقدوره، والعجز من أمارات الحدث وهو منافى للربوبية، وفيما ألزم هو الأمر بخلافه على ما قررنا.

?
You affirm that injustice is impossible for Allah because His action is eternally just. ?
If Allah's justice is eternal and cannot be removed, how does that reality confront your own excuses for your shortcuts and compromises? What would change in your daily interactions if you truly believed that every act of injustice is a violation of the very nature of your Creator?
?
The passage says that Allah's action is not only just but also beneficent (إفضال). When was the last time you extended beneficence to someone who deserved your justice but received your mercy instead? Will you commit this week to go beyond fairness and show unwarranted kindness, reflecting that divine attribute?

6 min
Impossible vs. Possible Objects of Divine Power
Al-Nasafi distinguishes between negation of power over impossible vs. possible objects, critiques false analogy, and presents Ash'ari argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between the negation of power over impossible objects (muhal) and possible objects (mumkin), and the Ash'ari perspective on power over the impossible.

Core Idea
Negation of power over an impossible object is not incapacity; only negation over a possible object would indicate deficiency.

Imam al-Nasafi deepens the discussion by distinguishing between two scenarios: when power is absent because the object is inherently impossible, and when power is absent over a possible object. The former is no deficiency, the latter would be. He then critiques false analogies and presents the Ash'ari position on power over the impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on power distinctions
Read the Arabic passage from 'فأما انتفاء القدرة عما هو مقدور في نفسه' to the end. Identify the two cases of negation of power.
Focus on the terms 'محال' and 'ممكن'.
2
Understand the two cases
First case: power is absent over an impossible object (like lying) — this does not imply incapacity. Second case: power is absent over a possible object — this would imply incapacity, which is a sign of contingency (hadath) and cannot apply to Allah.
Al-Nasafi uses the example of motion, life, and blackness not being receptive to power in inanimate objects to draw a contrast.
3
Analyze the critique of false analogy
Al-Nasafi criticizes those who analogize the absence of contingent attributes (like motion from a stone) to the absence of lying from Allah. The key difference is that lying is inherently impossible for reception of power, whereas motion is not inherently impossible; it is just that the subject (stone) is not receptive. This confuses the impossible with the possible.
This illustrates the importance of correct qiyas (analogy) in kalam.
4
Study the Ash'ari argument
Al-Nasafi presents the Ash'ari view: power over the impossible (like injustice) is impossible because injustice would entail subjecting Allah to another's authority, which contradicts lordship. The negation of power here is not due to incapacity but because the object is impossible.
This aligns with the earlier reasoning but from a different angle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فكان هذا من صاحبه تعجيزا له وكذا على القلب، فأما وجود الكذب من الباري عز وجل ففي حيز المستحيلات لما أن صدقه تعالى أزلي ممتنع العدم (ولا وجه لوجود كذبه مع وجود صدقه لاستحالة اجتماعهما) ولا وجه إلى القول بانعدام الصدق ليثبت الكذب لاستحالة العدم على الأزلي لكونه واجب الوجود وانتفاء القدرة) عما يستحيل دخوله تحت القدرة لا يكون عن عجز ، بل لخروج المحل عن أن يكون قابلا للقدرة فلا ثبوت للعجز الذي هو نقيصة منافية للقدم، فأما انتفاء القدرة عما هو مقدور في نفسه فلم يكن لامتناع المحل قبوله فكان لثبوت ما يضادها وهو العجز الذي هو من أمارات الحدث، فمن قاس خروج الحركة أو الحياة أو السواد ليس في أنفسها ما يمتنع عن قبول القدرة بخروج الكذب، مع أنه في نفسه ما يوجب امتناعه عن قبول القدرة فهو جاهل بشرائط القياس، غير بصير بالفرق بين المحال والممكن، وكذا صيرورة الظلم صفة الله تعالى محال لما أن فعله الأزلي عدل، وإفضال عندنا، ويمتنع قيام الظلم به مع وجود ذلك، ويستحيل على ذلك العدم، فكان محالا كما في الكذب، فأما في الحركة والسكون فالأمر بخلافه على ما بينا، وعند الأشعري فالقدرة على محال لما أن الظلم هو التعدي في الفعل عما جعل له، وارتكاب المنهي، ولا نهي لأحد على الله تعالى، فالقدرة على الظلم تستحيل، لأنها قدرة على إثبات ولاية الأمر والنهي لغير الله تعالى عليه، وإدخاله تحت قهر غيره، وهذا كله محال ممتنع ، فأما ما ألزمنا فليس بممتنع في نفسه، فكان انتفاء القدرة عن عجز فيه وقهر لصاحبه عليه حيث منعه عن إثبات مقدوره، والعجز من أمارات الحدث وهو منافى للربوبية، وفيما ألزم هو الأمر بخلافه على ما قررنا.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that any lack of power in Allah is a deficiency.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the negation of power over a possible object (maqdur fi nafsihi) indicate?
A) That the object is impossible.
B) Incapacity (cajz), which is a sign of contingency.
C) That the agent is all-powerful.
D) That the object is eternal.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider a prayer you have been afraid to make because you thought it was 'too impossible' for Allah to answer. After learning that impossibility is not a limitation of His power, will you still withhold that prayer? What would change if you truly believed that nothing is impossible for Him except what He has declared impossible (like shirk)?
?
Reflect on a sin you struggle with. Do you ever secretly think that Allah cannot forgive you because of its severity? How does the distinction between what is impossible for Allah (like injustice) and what is only difficult for you confront your hopelessness? Will you bring that sin to Him today, trusting that His power is not bounded by your past?
?
When you see others attribute limits to Allah—like saying 'God can't be involved in my life' or 'That's too big for God'—do you recognize those as echoes of the false analogy the passage warns against? How can you actively reject such thoughts in your own heart and replace them with the knowledge that only the impossible is impossible for Him?

Divine Will and the Generality of Action
Refutation of a doubt about the basis of the generality of divine will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidis affirm the generality of divine will over all created things and how it is based on the generality of action, not on knowledge.

Core Idea
Divine will is general because all actions are created by Allah and will makes actions voluntary.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi addresses a common misunderstanding about the Maturidi doctrine of divine will. Some critics claim that the Maturidis consider will to be identical to knowledge, leading to the conclusion that will is general because knowledge is general. Nasafi clarifies that will is actually attached to actions, not to God's essence or attributes. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping the Maturidi position on qadar and the nature of divine acts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the dense argumentation and the reference to a doubt (shubhah).
The passage is a refutation of a specific objection.
2
Identify the doubt being refuted
Find where Nasafi states the second doubt: that the Maturidis limit the discussion of will to those who affirm its generality, and that they base this on will not differing from knowledge.
This doubt is introduced at the beginning: 'فأما الشبهة الثانية'.
3
Understand the clarification
Nasafi explains that the Maturidis do not affirm generality of will because of generality of knowledge. Rather, will corresponds to action (fi'l) and makes an action voluntary. Since all actions are created by Allah, His will covers them all.
Key phrase: 'فالإرادة عندهم موافقة للفعل'.
4
Note the pedagogical simplification
At the end, Nasafi mentions that the simplified statement 'will corresponds to knowledge' was a concession for beginners. The true doctrine is as he has explained.
This shows the care Maturidi scholars took in teaching.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما الشبهة الثانية وهى أن الاختلاف في الإرادة غير مقصور على قول من يقول بعموم الإرادة في الكائنات لأن الإرادة عندهم لا تخالف العلم فنقول لو لم يكن ذلك متصورا لما أبطل الله تعالى قول الثنوية ولا أثبت وحدانيته بما تلونا من الآيات. ثم نقول لهم: إن إيراد هذه الشبهة صدر عن جهلكم بمذاهب خصومكم، وذلك أن القائلين بعموم الإرادة في الكائنات لم يقولوا بعمومها لعموم العلم ومو الإرادة العلم لأن عندهم علم الله تعالى يتعلق بذاته وصفاته ولا تتعلق إرادته بذلك، فإن الله تعالى يعلم ذاته وصفاته ولا يقال يريد ذاته وصفاته لتعلق الإرادة بالحوادث دون ما هو أزلي، فإذا الإرادة عندهم موافقة للفعل إذ بها يخرج الفعل عن حد الاضطرار إلى حد الاختيار، والله تعالى يفعل باختياره فكان جميع ما فعله الله فعله بإرادته، فكان القول بعموم الإرادة في الكائنات ( ) عندهم لعموم الفعل عندهم في الكائنات، لأن مذهبهم أن الحوادث كلها حدثت بإحداث الله تعالى وتخليقه إذ ليس لغيره قدرة التخليق، فكان القول بذلك قولا بعموم الإرادة لاستحالة امتياز إرادته عن فعله لامتناع كونه مضطرا في أفعاله، ولهذا قال الشيخ الإمام أبو منصور رحمه الله -: إن القول بإرادة العاصي تابع للقول بخلق الأفعال فإذا ثبت أنها مخلوقة الله تعالى ليس بمضطر في تخليقه كان ما هو مخلوقه مرادا له، وقولهم إن الإرادة توافق العلم دون الأمر، خرج على طريق المساهلة تيسيرا على المتعلمين، فأما حقيقة المذهب فعلى ما قررنا ، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك فلو كان
As for the second doubt: that the difference concerning will is not restricted to the saying of those who say that the will is general over all created things, because according to them the will does not differ from knowledge. So we say: If that were not conceivable, then Allah would not have refuted the saying of the Dualists nor established His unity by the verses we have recited. Then we say to them: The introduction of this doubt stems from your ignorance of the doctrines of your opponents. That is because those who affirm the generality of the will over all created things did not affirm its generality due to the generality of knowledge and [؟] will knowledge? Because according to them, Allah's knowledge pertains to His essence and attributes, but His will does not pertain to that. Indeed, Allah knows His essence and attributes, and it is not said that He wills His essence and attributes because will is attached to events and not to what is eternal. So the will according to them corresponds to the action, for through it the action exits from the limit of compulsion to the limit of choice. Allah acts by His choice, so everything that Allah has done, He has done by His will. So the saying that the will is general over all created things ( ) according to them is due to the generality of action according to them over all created things, because their doctrine is that all events occurred by Allah's causing and creation, for no one else has the power of creation. So the saying of that is a saying of the generality of the will, because it is impossible to distinguish His will from His action, because He is not compelled in His actions. For this reason, the Imam, Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The saying concerning the will of the disobedient is dependent on the saying concerning the creation of actions. So if it is established that they are created by Allah, and He is not compelled in His creation, then what He creates is willed by Him. And their saying that the will corresponds to knowledge and not to command is an approach of leniency to facilitate for the learners. As for the reality of the doctrine, it is as we have established. And if the matter is so, then if it were...
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage addresses a second doubt (shubhah) raised against the Maturidi doctrine of the generality of divine will (irada). The doubt claims that the Maturidis say the will is general because it follows knowledge (ilm), implying that will and knowledge are identical. Al-Nasafi first responds by pointing out that if this were not conceivable, then the Qur'anic verses refuting the Dualists and affirming God's unity would be meaningless, since those verses use the argument from volition. Then he clarifies the Maturidi position: those who affirm the generality of will do not do so because of the generality of knowledge, because knowledge pertains to God's essence and attributes, but will does not—God knows His essence but does not will it. Rather, will corresponds to action (fi'l); through will, an action becomes voluntary (ikhtiyari) rather than compelled (idtirari). Since Allah does all actions by His choice, all His actions are willed. Therefore, the generality of will is derived from the generality of action: all events are created by Allah alone, so they must be willed by Him. Al-Nasafi quotes Abu Mansur al-Maturidi: the will of the disobedient is dependent on the creation of actions—if actions are created by Allah, then He wills them. The passage ends by noting that the simplified statement that 'will corresponds to knowledge not to command' was a pedagogical simplification for beginners, but the true doctrine is as explained here.

Key Terms
إرادة
علم
فعل
اختيار
اضطرار
خلق الأفعال
عموم
شبهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that the Maturidis affirm the generality of divine will because they identify will with knowledge, leading to an equation of the two attributes.
Correction: The Maturidis do not base the generality of will on knowledge; rather, will is attached to actions, and since all actions are created by Allah, His will covers them all.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do the Maturidis affirm that the divine will is general over all created things?
A) Because the will is identical to knowledge and knowledge is general.
B) Because all actions are created by Allah and will is the attribute that makes actions voluntary.
C) Because the Qur'an uses the argument from will against the Dualists.
D) Because human will is general, and divine will must be more general.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi position on the generality of divine will is grounded in the fact that all actions are created by Allah, and will is the attribute that makes actions voluntary, not a mere reflection of knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If everything you do is created by Allah and willed by Him, how can you truly repent for your sins? Does this passage give you a way to reconcile divine will with personal responsibility?
?
Read Qur'anic verses that use the argument from will to prove God's unity—like the ones Nasafi references. Do you feel the weight of that argument in your heart, or do you take it as merely intellectual?
?
The passage says that without will, actions would be compelled. Have you ever felt your faith or obedience was compelled by fear or habit rather than genuine choice? What would it mean for you to act with real voluntary submission to Allah?

The Second Doubt: Will and Knowledge
Nasafi introduces the second doubt and provides the initial clarifications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second doubt regarding the universality of divine will and the initial clarification that will is tied to action, not knowledge.

Core Idea
Will is about action, not knowledge; universal will follows from universal action.

This lesson introduces a key doubt raised by opponents: that the Maturidi position on universal will is based on universal knowledge. The text shows why this is a misunderstanding and clarifies that will pertains to action, not to what is eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once. It presents the doubt and the initial response.
Note the phrase 'لو لم يكن ذلك متصورا'.
2
Identify the doubt
The doubt claims that difference in will is not limited to those who affirm universal will because will does not differ from knowledge.
They argue that if will and knowledge are the same, then universal will would follow from universal knowledge.
3
Understand the response
The response begins by pointing out that if difference in will were inconceivable, God would not have refuted the dualists using verses about difference in will.
This shows that difference in will is indeed conceivable.
4
Notice the key distinction
The text explains that will is not like knowledge: knowledge pertains to essence and attributes, but will only pertains to temporal events. Will makes action voluntary.
Thus, universality of will is based on universality of action, not knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما الشبهة الثانية وهى أن الاختلاف في الإرادة غير مقصور على قول من يقول بعموم الإرادة في الكائنات لأن الإرادة عندهم لا تخالف العلم فنقول لو لم يكن ذلك متصورا لما أبطل الله تعالى قول الثنوية ولا أثبت وحدانيته بما تلونا من الآيات. ثم نقول لهم: إن إيراد هذه الشبهة صدر عن جهلكم بمذاهب خصومكم، وذلك أن القائلين بعموم الإرادة في الكائنات لم يقولوا بعمومها لعموم العلم ومو الإرادة العلم لأن عندهم علم الله تعالى يتعلق بذاته وصفاته ولا تتعلق إرادته بذلك، فإن الله تعالى يعلم ذاته وصفاته ولا يقال يريد ذاته وصفاته لتعلق الإرادة بالحوادث دون ما هو أزلي، فإذا الإرادة عندهم موافقة للفعل إذ بها يخرج الفعل عن حد الاضطرار إلى حد الاختيار، والله تعالى يفعل باختياره فكان جميع ما فعله الله فعله بإرادته، فكان القول بعموم الإرادة في الكائنات ( ) عندهم لعموم الفعل عندهم في الكائنات، لأن مذهبهم أن الحوادث كلها حدثت بإحداث الله تعالى وتخليقه إذ ليس لغيره قدرة التخليق، فكان القول بذلك قولا بعموم الإرادة لاستحالة امتياز إرادته عن فعله لامتناع كونه مضطرا في أفعاله، ولهذا قال الشيخ الإمام أبو منصور رحمه الله: إن القول بإرادة العاصي تابع للقول بخلق الأفعال فإذا ثبت أنها مخلوقة الله تعالى ليس بمضطر في تخليقه كان ما هو مخلوقه مرادا له، وقولهم إن الإرادة توافق العلم دون الأمر، خرج على طريق المساهلة تيسيرا على المتعلمين، فأما حقيقة المذهب فعلى ما قررنا، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك فلو كان خالق آخر وكان ما يخلقه ذلك غير متعلق بفعله لم يكن متعلقا بإرادته فيتصور الاختلاف بينهما في الإرادة، كما يتصور الاختلاف عندكم بين الله تعالى وبين العبد في الإرادة لكون أفعال العباد خارجة عن فعله، وكان خروجها عن إرادته جائزا. لو سلكت هذه الطريقة لبطل كلامه واضمحل اعتراضه، والشيخ أبو الحسن الرستغفنى رحمه الله ذكر في كتابه المسمى بالإرشاد، أن الإلزام من حيث القدرة لا من حيث الإرادة غير ممكن لكن لما فيه من امتناع الاختلاف بينهما في الإرادة، وكذا أبو إسحاق الأسفراييني ذكر ما ذكر كلام أبي هاشم فقال: وليس هذا وجه الاستدلال به لكنه ما قدمنا في تحقيق القدرة ونفي النقيصة، ثم يرتقي منه إلى الإرادة، فهذا منه أيضا تسليم أن حقيقة الإلزام في إثبات القدرة دون الإرادة، فيبقى الإشكال، إن الله أثبت الاختلاف في الإرادة، ولو لم يكن متصورا لما ثبت ذلك على ما مر ذكره فنقول وبالله التوفيق إن من المعلوم الذي لا ريب فيه أن الاستدلال بقوله تعالى: لَفَسَدَنَا وبقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَعَلَا بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَى بَعْضٍ هو الاستدلال بنفاذ قدرة كل منهم، لما أن كلا منهم يفعل غير ما يفعل من وراءه من الآلهة، وتنفذ قدرته فيما يوجب علو أمره وظهور ملكه وسلطانه، وكذا بقوله تعالى: ﴿ قُلْ أَرَيْتُمْ إِنْ أَخَذَ اللَّهُ سَمَعَكُمْ وَأَبْصَرَكُمْ
As for the second doubt, which is that difference in will is not confined to the statement of one who says universal will in contingent things because will according to them does not differ from knowledge. We say: If that were not conceivable, then God Almighty would not have invalidated the statement of the dualists nor established His oneness by the verses we have recited. Then we say to them: The raising of this doubt stems from your ignorance of the doctrines of your opponents. That is because those who affirm universal will in contingent things did not affirm its universality due to the universality of knowledge — and will is [not?] knowledge — because according to them the knowledge of God Almighty pertains to His essence and attributes, but His will does not pertain to that. Indeed God Almighty knows His essence and attributes, but it is not said that He wills His essence and attributes, because will pertains to temporal events, not to what is eternal. Thus will according to them is appropriate for action, since by it action moves from the limit of compulsion to the limit of choice. God Almighty acts by His choice, so all that God did, He did by His will. So the statement of universal will in contingent things ( ) according to them is due to the universality of action for them in contingent things, because their doctrine is that all temporal events occur by the bringing-into-existence and creation of God Almighty, since no other has the power of creation. So that statement is a statement of universal will because of the impossibility of distinguishing His will from His action, due to the impossibility of His being compelled in His actions. For this reason the Shaykh al-Imam Abu Mansur (may God have mercy on him) said: 'The statement of the will of the disobedient is dependent on the statement of the creation of actions. So when it is established that they are created by God Almighty, He is not compelled in His creation, so whatever He creates is willed by Him.' And their statement that will conforms to knowledge and not to command was issued by way of facilitation for the learners. As for the reality of the doctrine, it is as we have established. When this is the case, if there were another creator, and what that one creates is not related to His action, it would not be related to His will. Thus difference between them in will would be conceivable, just as difference between God Almighty and the servant in will is conceivable according to you, because the actions of servants are outside His action, and their being outside His will is possible. If you followed this method, his speech would be invalidated and his objection would collapse. And Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani (may God have mercy on him) mentioned in his book called al-Irshad that the implication from the perspective of power, not from the perspective of will, is not possible, but because of the impossibility of difference between them in will. Likewise Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini mentioned what was mentioned of Abu Hashim's speech and said: 'This is not the aspect of inference with it, but rather it is what we advanced in establishing power and negating deficiency, then he ascends from it to will.' This from him is also a concession that the reality of the implication is in establishing power, not will, so the problem remains: God established difference in will, and if it were not conceivable, He would not have established it as mentioned earlier. So we say, and with God is success: It is among the known matters about which there is no doubt that the inference by His statement, the Exalted, 'they would have corrupted' and by His statement, the Exalted, 'and some of them would have risen above others', is inference by the penetration of the power of each of them, because each of them does something different from what the gods behind him do, and his power penetrates in what necessitates the loftiness of his command and the appearance of his kingdom and authority. Likewise by His statement, the Exalted, 'Say: Have you considered if God took away your hearing and your sight...'
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a response to a second doubt (shubha) regarding the universality of divine will. The doubt claims that difference in will is not limited to the position of those who affirm universal will for all contingent things (al-qa'ilin bi 'umum al-irada fi al-ka'inaat), because will, according to them, does not differ from knowledge. The author first points out that if such difference were inconceivable, then God would not have refuted the dualists (thunawiyya) and proven His oneness through the verses cited. He then explains that the doubt arises from ignorance of the opponents' doctrines. The proponents of universal will do not base it on the universality of knowledge, because while God's knowledge pertains to His essence and attributes, His will does not. Will only relates to temporal events (hawadith), not eternal matters. Moreover, will is tied to action, as it distinguishes voluntary action from compulsion. Since God acts by choice, all His acts are by His will. Thus, the universality of will follows from the universality of God's creative action, as He creates all events and no other has the power of creation. The author cites Abu Mansur al-Maturidi's statement that affirming the will of the disobedient is dependent on affirming the creation of actions. The earlier concession that will conforms to knowledge rather than command was only for pedagogical ease; the true doctrine is as stated. The author then considers the hypothetical case of another creator: if such a being existed, its actions would not be related to God's will, so difference in will would be conceivable, just as difference between God and human servants is conceivable because servants' actions are not created by God. The author references Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani and Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, who argue that the real proof is from power (qudra), not will, and that the argument from difference in will ultimately rests on power. Finally, the author asserts that the Quranic verses (Q21:22, Q23:91, Q6:46) invoked in the doubt actually prove difference in power, and thus the objection collapses.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha, doubt)
إرادة (irada, will)
علم ('ilm, knowledge)
فعل (fi'l, action)
اضطرار (idtirar, compulsion)
اختيار (ikhtiyar, choice)
ثنوية (thunawiyya, dualists)
كوائن (ka'inaat, contingent things)
حوادث (hawadith, temporal events)
تخليق (takhlīq, creation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Maturidis affirm universal will because God's knowledge is universal.
Correction: The text explains that will is not based on knowledge; it is based on action. Knowledge includes eternal attributes, but will only relates to temporal events.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do the proponents of universal will affirm that God's will is universal?
A) Because God's knowledge encompasses all things, so His will must also encompass all things.
B) Because God's action is universal, and He acts by choice, so everything He does is willed.
C) Because will and knowledge are identical in God, so universality of knowledge implies universality of will.
D) Because God wills His own essence and attributes, which are eternal.

Key Takeaway
Universal will is tied to universal action, not universal knowledge; God's will pertains to temporal events, not His essence or attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face trials, do you ever doubt that God's will is truly active in every moment, or do you subconsciously think He is distant? How does the lesson's emphasis that God's will is tied to His actions — all of them — change your perspective on your current struggles?
?
You believe God knows everything, but do you live as if He also wills everything that happens to you? If you truly accepted that His will is inseparable from His action, what worry or regret would you have to surrender today?
?
The lesson reveals that God does not will His own essence — His will is entirely directed outward to creation. How does this reframe your understanding of God's care for you? Are you relying on His will as the basis for your choices, or are you still trying to act as if you are the master of your own fate?

The Maturidi Principle: Will Follows Action
Nasafi cites Imam Maturidi and clarifies the pedagogical concession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that affirming the will of the disobedient is dependent on the creation of actions, and that the Maturidi school's true doctrine is based on this principle.

Core Idea
Will is dependent on action; since God creates all actions, He wills them.

This lesson presents the authoritative statement of Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, tying the will of the disobedient to the creation of actions. It also clarifies that a previous statement about will conforming to knowledge was a pedagogical concession, not the actual doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read Maturidi's statement
Read the passage from 'ولهذا قال الشيخ الإمام أبو منصور رحمه الله' to 'فأما حقيقة المذهب فعلى ما قررنا'.
This is the core of the Maturidi position.
2
Understand the link between will and creation
Maturidi states that saying the disobedient person wills is dependent on saying that actions are created by God. If actions are created by God, then God wills them, because He is not compelled in His creation.
Thus, God's will is universal because His action is universal.
3
Note the pedagogical concession
The text mentions that some said will conforms to knowledge as a facilitation for learners, but the reality is as established.
This shows the difference between simplified teaching and the actual doctrine.
4
Grasp the real doctrine
The real doctrine is that will is tied to action, and since all actions are created by God, He wills all of them.
This refutes the doubt that universal will is based on knowledge.

القول بإرادة العاصي تابع للقول بخلق الأفعال فإذا ثبت أنها مخلوقة الله تعالى ليس بمضطر في تخليقه كان ما هو مخلوقه مرادا له، وقولهم إن الإرادة توافق العلم دون الأمر، خرج على طريق المساهلة تيسيرا على المتعلمين، فأما حقيقة المذهب فعلى ما قررنا، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك فلو كان خالق آخر وكان ما يخلقه ذلك غير متعلق بفعله لم يكن متعلقا بإرادته فيتصور الاختلاف بينهما في الإرادة، كما يتصور الاختلاف عندكم بين الله تعالى وبين العبد في الإرادة لكون أفعال العباد خارجة عن فعله، وكان خروجها عن إرادته جائزا. لو سلكت هذه الطريقة لبطل كلامه واضمحل اعتراضه، والشيخ أبو الحسن الرستغفنى رحمه الله ذكر في كتابه المسمى بالإرشاد، أن الإلزام من حيث القدرة لا من حيث الإرادة غير ممكن لكن لما فيه من امتناع الاختلاف بينهما في الإرادة، وكذا أبو إسحاق الأسفراييني ذكر ما ذكر كلام أبي هاشم فقال: وليس هذا وجه الاستدلال به لكنه ما قدمنا في تحقيق القدرة ونفي النقيصة، ثم يرتقي منه إلى الإرادة، فهذا منه أيضا تسليم أن حقيقة الإلزام في إثبات القدرة دون الإرادة، فيبقى الإشكال، إن الله أثبت الاختلاف في الإرادة، ولو لم يكن متصورا لما ثبت ذلك على ما مر ذكره فنقول وبالله التوفيق إن من المعلوم الذي لا ريب فيه أن الاستدلال بقوله تعالى: لَفَسَدَنَا وبقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَعَلَا بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَى بَعْضٍ هو الاستدلال بنفاذ قدرة كل منهم، لما أن كلا منهم يفعل غير ما يفعل من وراءه من الآلهة، وتنفذ قدرته فيما يوجب علو أمره وظهور ملكه وسلطانه، وكذا بقوله تعالى: ﴿ قُلْ أَرَيْتُمْ إِنْ أَخَذَ اللَّهُ سَمَعَكُمْ وَأَبْصَرَكُمْ
As for the second doubt, which is that difference in will is not confined to the statement of one who says universal will in contingent things because will according to them does not differ from knowledge. We say: If that were not conceivable, then God Almighty would not have invalidated the statement of the dualists nor established His oneness by the verses we have recited. Then we say to them: The raising of this doubt stems from your ignorance of the doctrines of your opponents. That is because those who affirm universal will in contingent things did not affirm its universality due to the universality of knowledge — and will is [not?] knowledge — because according to them the knowledge of God Almighty pertains to His essence and attributes, but His will does not pertain to that. Indeed God Almighty knows His essence and attributes, but it is not said that He wills His essence and attributes, because will pertains to temporal events, not to what is eternal. Thus will according to them is appropriate for action, since by it action moves from the limit of compulsion to the limit of choice. God Almighty acts by His choice, so all that God did, He did by His will. So the statement of universal will in contingent things ( ) according to them is due to the universality of action for them in contingent things, because their doctrine is that all temporal events occur by the bringing-into-existence and creation of God Almighty, since no other has the power of creation. So that statement is a statement of universal will because of the impossibility of distinguishing His will from His action, due to the impossibility of His being compelled in His actions. For this reason the Shaykh al-Imam Abu Mansur (may God have mercy on him) said: 'The statement of the will of the disobedient is dependent on the statement of the creation of actions. So when it is established that they are created by God Almighty, He is not compelled in His creation, so whatever He creates is willed by Him.' And their statement that will conforms to knowledge and not to command was issued by way of facilitation for the learners. As for the reality of the doctrine, it is as we have established. When this is the case, if there were another creator, and what that one creates is not related to His action, it would not be related to His will. Thus difference between them in will would be conceivable, just as difference between God Almighty and the servant in will is conceivable according to you, because the actions of servants are outside His action, and their being outside His will is possible. If you followed this method, his speech would be invalidated and his objection would collapse. And Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani (may God have mercy on him) mentioned in his book called al-Irshad that the implication from the perspective of power, not from the perspective of will, is not possible, but because of the impossibility of difference between them in will. Likewise Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini mentioned what was mentioned of Abu Hashim's speech and said: 'This is not the aspect of inference with it, but rather it is what we advanced in establishing power and negating deficiency, then he ascends from it to will.' This from him is also a concession that the reality of the implication is in establishing power, not will, so the problem remains: God established difference in will, and if it were not conceivable, He would not have established it as mentioned earlier. So we say, and with God is success: It is among the known matters about which there is no doubt that the inference by His statement, the Exalted, 'they would have corrupted' and by His statement, the Exalted, 'and some of them would have risen above others', is inference by the penetration of the power of each of them, because each of them does something different from what the gods behind him do, and his power penetrates in what necessitates the loftiness of his command and the appearance of his kingdom and authority. Likewise by His statement, the Exalted, 'Say: Have you considered if God took away your hearing and your sight...'
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a response to a second doubt (shubha) regarding the universality of divine will. The doubt claims that difference in will is not limited to the position of those who affirm universal will for all contingent things (al-qa'ilin bi 'umum al-irada fi al-ka'inaat), because will, according to them, does not differ from knowledge. The author first points out that if such difference were inconceivable, then God would not have refuted the dualists (thunawiyya) and proven His oneness through the verses cited. He then explains that the doubt arises from ignorance of the opponents' doctrines. The proponents of universal will do not base it on the universality of knowledge, because while God's knowledge pertains to His essence and attributes, His will does not. Will only relates to temporal events (hawadith), not eternal matters. Moreover, will is tied to action, as it distinguishes voluntary action from compulsion. Since God acts by choice, all His acts are by His will. Thus, the universality of will follows from the universality of God's creative action, as He creates all events and no other has the power of creation. The author cites Abu Mansur al-Maturidi's statement that affirming the will of the disobedient is dependent on affirming the creation of actions. The earlier concession that will conforms to knowledge rather than command was only for pedagogical ease; the true doctrine is as stated. The author then considers the hypothetical case of another creator: if such a being existed, its actions would not be related to God's will, so difference in will would be conceivable, just as difference between God and human servants is conceivable because servants' actions are not created by God. The author references Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani and Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, who argue that the real proof is from power (qudra), not will, and that the argument from difference in will ultimately rests on power. Finally, the author asserts that the Quranic verses (Q21:22, Q23:91, Q6:46) invoked in the doubt actually prove difference in power, and thus the objection collapses.

Key Terms
إرادة (irada, will)
خلق (khalq, creation)
أفعال (af'al, actions)
اختيار (ikhtiyar, choice)
مضطر (mudtar, compelled)
مساهلة (musahala, facilitation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Maturidis believe will conforms to knowledge in reality.
Correction: The text explains that this was said as a facilitation; the real doctrine is that will is tied to action.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Maturidi as quoted, what is the will of the disobedient dependent on?
A) The disobedience itself.
B) The creation of actions.
C) God's knowledge of the action.
D) The command of God.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi school's true doctrine is that God wills all actions because He creates them, and this is not based on knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly believe that God willed that act even as He forbids it? How does this dual truth affect your view of His mercy and your accountability?
?
The passage says God is not compelled in His creation. Reflect on a recent choice you made. Can you honestly say you felt God's will behind it, or do you still cling to a sense of self-sufficiency? What would it mean to surrender that feeling?
?
Imam Maturidi’s facilitation was for beginners. Are you willing to move beyond comfortable simplifications and embrace the harder truths of your faith? What is one doctrine you have been avoiding because it challenges your assumptions?

Extending the Argument: Other Creators and Quranic Proof
Nasafi concludes the refutation with hypothetical reasoning and references to other scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the argument from difference in will can be extended to hypothetical other creators and how the Quranic verses ultimately prove difference in power.

Core Idea
Difference in will is conceivable when actions are separate; Quranic proof is about power, not will.

This lesson completes the refutation by considering the hypothetical scenario of another creator. The author shows that if such a being existed, its actions would not be related to God's will, so difference in will would be conceivable. Then references to other scholars are given, and finally the author asserts that the Quranic verses actually prove difference in power, not will.

Guided Path
1
Read the hypothetical scenario
Read from 'وإذا كان الأمر كذلك' to the end. The author imagines another creator whose actions are separate from God's.
This is a logical extension.
2
Understand the logical consequence
If another creator's actions are not related to God's action, then they are not willed by God, so difference in will is conceivable.
This parallels the difference between God and human servants.
3
Note the scholars' comments
Al-Rustughfani and al-Isfarayini note that the real implication is from power, not will.
They concede that the argument ultimately rests on power.
4
Understand the Quranic inference
The verses quoted (Q21:22, Q23:91, Q6:46) actually prove the penetration of power of each deity, not a difference in will per se.
Thus the doubt is refuted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما الشبهة الثانية وهى أن الاختلاف في الإرادة غير مقصور على قول من يقول بعموم الإرادة في الكائنات لأن الإرادة عندهم لا تخالف العلم فنقول لو لم يكن ذلك متصورا لما أبطل الله تعالى قول الثنوية ولا أثبت وحدانيته بما تلونا من الآيات. ثم نقول لهم: إن إيراد هذه الشبهة صدر عن جهلكم بمذاهب خصومكم، وذلك أن القائلين بعموم الإرادة في الكائنات لم يقولوا بعمومها لعموم العلم ومو الإرادة العلم لأن عندهم علم الله تعالى يتعلق بذاته وصفاته ولا تتعلق إرادته بذلك، فإن الله تعالى يعلم ذاته وصفاته ولا يقال يريد ذاته وصفاته لتعلق الإرادة بالحوادث دون ما هو أزلي، فإذا الإرادة عندهم موافقة للفعل إذ بها يخرج الفعل عن حد الاضطرار إلى حد الاختيار، والله تعالى يفعل باختياره فكان جميع ما فعله الله فعله بإرادته، فكان القول بعموم الإرادة في الكائنات ( ) عندهم لعموم الفعل عندهم في الكائنات، لأن مذهبهم أن الحوادث كلها حدثت بإحداث الله تعالى وتخليقه إذ ليس لغيره قدرة التخليق، فكان القول بذلك قولا بعموم الإرادة لاستحالة امتياز إرادته عن فعله لامتناع كونه مضطرا في أفعاله، ولهذا قال الشيخ الإمام أبو منصور رحمه الله: إن القول بإرادة العاصي تابع للقول بخلق الأفعال فإذا ثبت أنها مخلوقة الله تعالى ليس بمضطر في تخليقه كان ما هو مخلوقه مرادا له، وقولهم إن الإرادة توافق العلم دون الأمر، خرج على طريق المساهلة تيسيرا على المتعلمين، فأما حقيقة المذهب فعلى ما قررنا، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك فلو كان خالق آخر وكان ما يخلقه ذلك غير متعلق بفعله لم يكن متعلقا بإرادته فيتصور الاختلاف بينهما في الإرادة، كما يتصور الاختلاف عندكم بين الله تعالى وبين العبد في الإرادة لكون أفعال العباد خارجة عن فعله، وكان خروجها عن إرادته جائزا. لو سلكت هذه الطريقة لبطل كلامه واضمحل اعتراضه، والشيخ أبو الحسن الرستغفنى رحمه الله ذكر في كتابه المسمى بالإرشاد، أن الإلزام من حيث القدرة لا من حيث الإرادة غير ممكن لكن لما فيه من امتناع الاختلاف بينهما في الإرادة، وكذا أبو إسحاق الأسفراييني ذكر ما ذكر كلام أبي هاشم فقال: وليس هذا وجه الاستدلال به لكنه ما قدمنا في تحقيق القدرة ونفي النقيصة، ثم يرتقي منه إلى الإرادة، فهذا منه أيضا تسليم أن حقيقة الإلزام في إثبات القدرة دون الإرادة، فيبقى الإشكال، إن الله أثبت الاختلاف في الإرادة، ولو لم يكن متصورا لما ثبت ذلك على ما مر ذكره فنقول وبالله التوفيق إن من المعلوم الذي لا ريب فيه أن الاستدلال بقوله تعالى: لَفَسَدَنَا وبقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَعَلَا بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَى بَعْضٍ هو الاستدلال بنفاذ قدرة كل منهم، لما أن كلا منهم يفعل غير ما يفعل من وراءه من الآلهة، وتنفذ قدرته فيما يوجب علو أمره وظهور ملكه وسلطانه، وكذا بقوله تعالى: ﴿ قُلْ أَرَيْتُمْ إِنْ أَخَذَ اللَّهُ سَمَعَكُمْ وَأَبْصَرَكُمْ

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
